-۱۷ ورواية الحسن بأن الحرة العاقلة البالغة لو زوّجت نفسها من غير كُفْؤ لا يصح.
الاعتبار للعرف الحادث
۱۸ - وإفتاؤهم بالعفو عن طين الشارع للضرورة.
۱۹ ، ۲۰ - وببيع الوفاء، والاستصناع.
۲۱ - والشرب من السقاء بلا بيان مقدار ما يشرب.
۲۲ - ودخول الحمام بلا بيان مدة المكث، ومقدار ما يصب من الماء.
٢٣ واستقراض العجين والخبز بلا وزن. وغير ذلك مما بني على العرف. وقد ذكر من ذلك في "الأشباه" مسائل كثيرة. فهذه كلها قد تغيّرت أحكامها لتغير الزمان، إما للضرورة، وإما للعرف، وإما لقرائن الأحوال، وكل ذلك غير خارج عن المذهب؛ لأن صاحب المذهب لو كان في هذا الزمان لقال بها، ولو حدث هذا التغير في زمانه لم ينص على خلافها. وهذا الذي جرأ المجتهدين في المذهب، وأهل النظر الصحيح من المتأخرين على مخالفة المنصوص عليه من صاحب المذهب في كتب ظاهر الرواية، بناء على ما كان في زمنه، كما مر تصريحهم به في مسألة "كل حل عليّ حرام" من أن محمدا قاله على عرف زمانه وكذا ما قدمناه في الاستئجار على التعليم.
فإن قلت: العرف يتغيّر مرة بعد مرة، فلو حدث عرف آخر لم يقع في الزمان السابق، فهل يسوغ للمفتي مخالفة المنصوص واتباع العرف الحادث؟ قلت: نعم! فإن المتأخرين الذين خالفوا المنصوص في المسائل المارة، لم يخالفوه إلا لحدوث عُرف بعد زمن الإمام، فللمفتي اتباع عُرفه الحادث في الألفاظ العرفية، وكذا في الأحكام التي بناها المجتهد على ما
Explanation of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. Change of rulings by change of custom. 9 - And not hearing his statement that he made an exception after swearing by divorce except with evidence, even though it is contrary to the apparent narration, and they explained it by the corruption of the time. 10 - And not believing her after consummation that she did not receive the prompt dower stipulated for her, even though she denies receipt and the principle of the madhhab is that the word is of the denier, but usually she does not surrender herself before receiving it. 11 - And likewise they said in his statement 'Every halal upon me is haram' that divorce occurs by custom. The mashayikh of Balkh said: Muhammad's statement 'it does not occur except with intention' he answered according to the custom of their region. As for the custom of our lands, they mean by it the prohibition of the wife, so it is applied accordingly. 'Allamah Qasim transmitted it, and it is transmitted from 'Mukhtarat al-Nawazil' that the fatwa is upon it due to the predominance of usage by custom. Then he said: 'I say: the expressions and those used in this in our Egypt are: divorce is incumbent upon me, and haram is incumbent upon me, and upon me is divorce, and upon me is haram.' 12 - And likewise the case of the father's claim that he did not give the trousseau to his daughter; they based it on custom, even though the principle is that the word is of the one giving ownership regarding ownership and its absence. 13 - And likewise making the woman's word accepted regarding her deferred dower, even though the word is of the denier. 14, 15 - And likewise their statement: the chosen in our time is their statement in sharecropping, mu'amalah, and waqf due to necessity and general occurrence. 16 - And Muhammad's statement that pre-emption drops if he delays the request for ownership for a month, to ward off harm from the buyer. 17 - And the narration of Hasan that a free, sane, adult woman if she marries herself to a non-compatible (kufu) person, it is not valid. Consideration of the new custom. 18 - And their giving fatwa of pardon for mud of the street due to necessity. 19, 20 - And bay' al-wafa, and istisna'. 21 - And drinking from a water skin without specifying the amount drunk. 22 - And entering the bathhouse without specifying the duration of stay and the amount of water poured. 23 - And borrowing dough and bread without weight. And other things that are built on custom. Many such issues have been mentioned in 'al-Ashbah'. All these have had their rulings changed due to change of time, either due to necessity, or custom, or circumstances of conditions, and all that is not outside the madhhab; because the founder of the madhhab, if he were in this time, would have said them, and if this change had occurred in his time he would not have explicitly opposed them. And this is what emboldened the mujtahids in the madhhab and the people of sound consideration among the later scholars to oppose what is explicitly stated by the founder of the madhhab in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, based on what was in his time, as their explicit statement passed in the issue of 'Every halal upon me is haram' that Muhammad said it according to the custom of his time, and likewise what we presented on hiring for teaching. If you say: custom changes again and again, so if another custom occurs that did not exist in the previous time, is it permissible for the mufti to oppose the explicit text and follow the new custom? I say: Yes! For the later scholars who opposed the explicit text in the aforementioned issues only opposed it due to the occurrence of a custom after the Imam's time, so the mufti may follow his new custom in customary expressions, and likewise in the rulings that the mujtahid built upon.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the principle that rulings change with custom (taghayyur al-ahkam bi taghayyur al-urf). The author lists numerous examples where later Hanafi scholars issued rulings contrary to the explicit texts of Zahir al-Riwayah because of changes in custom or necessity. For instance, the denial of a husband's claim of exception after swearing divorce without evidence (no. 9) is justified by 'corruption of the time'. Similarly, the wife's denial of receiving prompt dower is not accepted after consummation because custom indicates she would not submit without payment (no. 10). In the case of the phrase 'every halal is haram', the Hanafi position that divorce occurs without intention is based on prevalent custom, and the mashayikh of Balkh explain that Imam Muhammad's contrary view was for their custom (no. 11). Other examples include the father's claim regarding trousseau, the wife's word on deferred dower, choice in sharecropping, pre-emption, etc. The author then introduces the principle of 'consideration of the new custom' (i'tibar al-urf al-hadith). He asserts that all these changes are within the madhhab because the founder would have ruled accordingly if he had lived in this time. This justifies later scholars opposing explicit texts from Zahir al-Riwayah when custom has changed. The passage concludes with a question-answer: if a new custom arises after the Imam's time, the mufti is permitted to follow the new custom over the explicit text, as did the later scholars.

Key Terms
العرف (al-'urf): Custom or prevailing practice in a particular time and place that influences legal rulings.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani containing the authoritative transmissions from Abu Hanifa and his students.
المتأخرون (al-muta'akhkhirun): Later Hanafi scholars after the time of the founding imams, who faced new customs and necessities.
فساد الزمان (fasad al-zaman): Corruption of the time, a justification for changing a ruling due to decline in people's honesty and religious adherence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did later Hanafi scholars oppose the explicit text of Zahir al-Riwayah in the issue of the statement 'every halal is haram'?
A) Because they found a stronger hadith.
B) Because the custom of their time interpreted the phrase as implying divorce, unlike the custom of Imam Muhammad's time.
C) Because they were not aware of the original ruling.
D) Because they considered all such oaths as divorce regardless of custom.

Key Takeaway
Custom is a legitimate basis for changing a ruling within the Hanafi school, even if it contradicts an earlier explicit text, provided the change is driven by a genuine shift in practice.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Maxim of New Custom in Fatwa
Rule for muftis: consider new custom even over explicit texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-`urf al-hadith' to identify when a mufti may depart from the explicit texts (manus) of the school based on changed custom, and state the qualifications required for such a departure.

Core Idea
New custom can override the explicit Hanafi text if the founder himself would have ruled differently today.

This lesson presents a fundamental rule in Hanafi fatwa methodology: the permissibility of following a new custom (`urf hadith) even when it contradicts the explicit rulings (manus) of the early Imams. We will study the evidence, the conditions, and the practical examples from the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
State the maxim 'al-i'tibar lil-`urf al-hadith' (Consideration is for the new custom) and note its rank as a wusta (intermediate) maxim governing fatwa and judicial rulings.
The maxim restricts adherence to explicit texts (manus) when custom has changed.
2
List the furu` (examples) from the passage
Identify the six concrete cases where muftis ruled according to new custom: pardoning mud, bay' al-wafa, istisna', drinking from waterskin, entering bathhouse, borrowing dough without weight. For each, note how the strict textual ruling was relaxed.
These examples show that custom can waive requirements like specification and measurement.
3
Understand the theoretical justification
The passage argues that the Imam (Abu Hanifa) would have ruled the same if he lived in the later time. This is not a departure from the madhhab but an application of its principles to changed circumstances.
The justification is that the founders' rulings were based on their own customs; when customs change, the ruling changes.
4
Recognize the conditions and qualifications
The mufti must have proper insight (`ra'y wa nazar sahih), knowledge of Shari`a principles, and training under a master. He must distinguish valid `urf from invalid ones, and custom must not contradict definitive texts of Quran and Sunnah.
The passage emphasizes that full ijtihad is absent today, so at minimum the mufti must know the conditions and restrictions of the rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتبار للعرف الحادث
18 - وإفتاؤهم بالعفو عن طين الشارع للضرورة.
19، 20 - وببيع الوفاء، والاستصناع.
21 - والشرب من السقاء بلا بيان مقدار ما يشرب.
22 - ودخول الحمام بلا بيان مدة المكث، ومقدار ما يصب من الماء.
23 - واستقراض العجين والخبز بلا وزن. وغير ذلك مما جرى به العرف. وقد ذكر من ذلك في "الأشباه" مسائل كثيرة. فهذه كلها قد تغيّرت أحكامها لتغير الزمان، إما للضرورة، وإما للعرف، وإما لقرائن الأحوال، وكل ذلك غير خارج عن المذهب؛ لأن صاحب المذهب لو كان في هذا الزمان لقال بها، ولو حدث هذا التغير في زمانه لم ينص على خلافها. وهذا الذي جرأ المجتهدين في المذهب، وأهل النظر الصحيح من المتأخرين على مخالفة المنصوص عليه من صاحب المذهب في كتب ظاهر الرواية، بناء على ما كان في زمنه، كما مر تصريحهم به في مسألة "كل حل علي حرام" من أن محمدا قاله على عرف زمانه، وكذا ما قدمناه في الاستئجار على التعليم.

فإن قلت: العرف يتغيّر مرة بعد مرة، فلو حدث عرف آخر لم يقع في الزمان السابق، فهل يسوغ للمفتي مخالفة المنصوص واتباع العرف الحادث؟ قلت: نعم! فإن المتأخرين الذين خالفوا المنصوص في المسائل المارة، لم يخالفوه إلا لحدوث عُرف بعد زمن الإمام، فللمفتي اتباع عُرفه الحادث في الألفاظ العرفية، وكذا في الأحكام التي بناها المجتهد على ما كان في عرف زمانه، وتغيّر عرفه إلى عرف آخر، اقتداء بهم. لكن بعد أن يكون المفتي ممن له رأي ونظر صحيح، ومعرفة بقواعد الشرع حتى يميز بين العرف الذي يجوز بناء الأحكام عليه وبين غيره؛ فإن المتقدمين شرطوا في المفتي الاجتهاد وهذا مفقود في زماننا، فلا أقل أن يشترط فيه معرفة المسائل بشروطها وقيودها التي كثيرا ما يسقطونها، ولا يصرحون بها اعتمادا على فهم المتفقه.

وكذا لا بد له من معرفة عرف زمانه وأحوال أهله، والتخرج في ذلك على أستاذ ماهر، ولذا قال في آخر "منية المفتي": لو أن الرجل حفظ جميع كتب أصحابنا لا بد أن يتلمذ للفتوى، حتى يهتدي إليه؛ لأن كثيرا من المسائل يجاب عنه على عادات أهل الزمان فيما لا يخالف الشريعة. وفي "القنية": ليس للمفتي ولا للقاضي أن يحكما على ظاهر المذهب ويتركا العرف. ونقل منها في "خزانة الروايات". وهذا صريح فيما قلنا: إن المفتي لا يفتي بخلاف عرف أهل زمانه. ويقرب منه ما نقله في "الأشباه" عن "البزازية" من أن المفتي يفتي بما يقع عنده. وكتبت في "رد المحتار" في باب القسامة فيما لو ادعى الولي على رجل من غير أهل المحلة، وشهد اثنان منهم عليه، لم تقبل عنده، وقالا: تقبل إلخ. نقل السيد الحموي عن العلامة المقدسي أنه قال: توقفت عن الفتوى بقول الإمام، ومنعت من إشاعته؛ لما يترتب عليه من الضرر العام، فإن من عرفه من المتمردين يتجاسر على قتل النفس في المحلات الخالية من أهلها، معتمدا على عدم قبول شهادتهم عليه حتى قلت: ينبغي الفتوى على قولهما، لا سيما والأحكام تختلف باختلاف الأيام.
Consideration of the new custom. 18 - And their issuing fatwa of pardoning the mud of the street due to necessity. 19, 20 - And [the validity of] bay' al-wafa and istisna'. 21 - And drinking from a waterskin without specifying the amount drunk. 22 - And entering a bathhouse without specifying the duration of stay and the amount of water poured. 23 - And borrowing dough and bread without weighing. And other such matters that custom has established. Many such issues have been mentioned in al-Ashbah. So all these have changed their rulings due to change of time, either due to necessity, or custom, or circumstantial evidence. And all that is not outside the madhhab; because if the founder of the madhhab were in this time, he would have said them, and if this change had occurred in his time, he would not have explicitly stated contrary. And this encouraged the mujtahids in the madhhab and those of correct insight among the later scholars to oppose what is explicitly stated by the founder of the madhhab in the works of Zahir al-Riwayah, based on what was in his time, as their explicit statement has passed in the issue 'All halal upon me is haram' that Muhammad said it according to the custom of his time, and likewise what we presented on hiring for teaching. For you say: Custom changes time after time; so if another custom occurs that did not exist in the previous time, is it permissible for the mufti to oppose the explicit text and follow the new custom? I say: Yes! Because the later scholars who opposed the explicit text in the mentioned cases only opposed it due to the occurrence of a custom after the Imam's time. So for the mufti it is permissible to follow his new custom in customary expressions, and similarly in the rulings that the mujtahid based on what was in the custom of his time, and his custom changed to another custom, following their example. But after the mufti is one who has opinion and correct insight, and knowledge of the principles of Shari'a, so that he can distinguish between the custom on which it is permissible to build rulings and other [customs]. Because the earlier scholars required ijtihad in the mufti, and this is absent in our time; so at the very least it is required that he know the issues with their conditions and restrictions which they often omit and do not explicitly state, relying on the understanding of the jurist. Likewise, he must know the custom of his time and the conditions of its people, and be trained in that under a proficient teacher. That is why it is said at the end of Munyat al-Mufti: 'If a man memorized all the books of our companions, he must still apprentice for fatwa until he is guided; because many issues are answered based on the customs of the people of the time in what does not contradict the Shari'a.' And in al-Qunyah: 'It is not for the mufti nor the judge to rule according to the apparent [meaning] of the madhhab and ignore custom.' And it is transmitted from it in Khizanat al-Riwayat. And this is clear in what we said: that the mufti does not issue fatwa contrary to the custom of the people of his time. And close to it is what is transmitted in al-Ashbah from al-Bazaziyya that the mufti issues fatwa according to what occurs to him. And I wrote in Radd al-Muhtar in the chapter of Qasama regarding a case where the guardian accuses a man not from the residents of the neighborhood, and two of them testify against him. It is not accepted according to him [Abu Hanifa] and they [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: it is accepted, etc. Al-Hamawi narrated from al-Maqdisi that he said: I refrained from giving fatwa according to the Imam's opinion and prevented its dissemination due to the general harm resulting from it; because those wrongdoers who know it would become bold to kill people in neighborhoods empty of their residents, relying on the non-acceptance of testimony against them. So I said: fatwa should be given according to their opinion [the Sahibayn], especially since rulings differ with the difference of days.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule for muftis: new customs (`urf hadith) are to be taken into account when issuing fatwas, even if they contradict the explicit texts (manus) of the earlier Hanafi masters. The author begins by listing practical examples where Hanafi muftis have ruled differently due to changed customs: pardoning mud on public roads (necessary for ease), validity of bay' al-wafa (a type of sale with repurchase agreement), istisna' (manufacturing contract), drinking from a waterskin without specifying quantity, entering a bathhouse without fixing duration or water amount, and borrowing unbaked dough or bread without weighing. These rulings depart from the strict requirement of specification (gharar prevention) but are justified by the custom of the people. The author asserts that such changes do not exit the Hanafi school because Imam Abu Hanifa himself would have ruled the same if he lived in this time; the change is due to changed circumstances, not a rejection of his method. This principle emboldened later mujtahids within the school to oppose the transmitted texts from Zahir al-Riwayah when the `urf shifted. A possible objection is raised: if customs change repeatedly, can a mufti always follow the new custom? The answer is yes, following the precedent of later scholars. However, the mufti must be qualified: he needs proper insight, knowledge of Shari'a principles, and ability to distinguish valid `urf from invalid ones. Since full ijtihad is absent today, he must at least know the conditions and restrictions of the issues he is asked about, and be well-versed in the contemporary customs by training under a skilled teacher. The text quotes two key works: from Munyat al-Mufti, that even one who memorizes all Hanafi books must apprentice; from al-Qunyah, that a mufti and judge cannot rule by literal madhhab while ignoring custom. A concrete example from Radd al-Muhtar illustrates this: in a murder case, Abu Hanifa's ruling that testimony of residents against a non-resident is not accepted caused potential harm (increased crime). Later scholars preferred the opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) to prevent public harm. This shows that rulings can change with changing circumstances and customs. The overarching message: a mufti must balance adherence to the madhhab with consideration of contemporary custom, public interest, and harm prevention.

Key Terms
العرف الحادث (al-`urf al-hadith): A custom that emerges after the time of the founding imams (particularly Abu Hanifa) and was not prevalent in their era, which justifies modifying or departing from their explicit rulings.
المنصوص (al-manus): The explicit textual ruling transmitted from the founders (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) in the works of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum requirement for a mufti to follow a new custom in his fatwa?
A) He must be a mujtahid mutlaq.
B) He must have knowledge of the issues with their conditions and restrictions, and training under a proficient teacher.
C) He must have memorized all six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
D) He must ignore the old customs entirely.

Key Takeaway
A mufti may follow a new custom over the explicit texts of the school, provided the custom does not contradict definitive Shari'a and the mufti possesses proper insight and training.

Custom and Its Limits in Fatwa
Explains that custom is upheld unless it contradicts shari'ah, with example from fasting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that custom is followed unless it contradicts shari'ah, and identify the mufti's role in assessing custom and individual conditions.

Core Idea
Custom is a source of fatwa only when it does not contradict shari'ah; the mufti must know people's conditions.

This passage from Sharh 'Uqood Rasm al-Mufti establishes a fundamental principle: custom ('urf) is a valid source for fatwa as long as it does not contradict explicit shari'ah texts. Through the example of eating meat between teeth while fasting, the author demonstrates how the mufti must exercise ijtihad and consider individual circumstances, choosing between the views of Abu Yusuf and Zufar based on the person's nature and custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling principle
Find the statement that custom is followed unless it contradicts shari'ah. Note the exact wording from the passage.
The principle is explicit at the end: 'العمل بالعرف ما لم يخالف الشريعة'.
2
Examine the example from fasting
Review the ruling from al-Hidayah about meat between teeth and the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Zufar.
Abu Yusuf distinguishes based on quantity; Zufar says breaks in both cases.
3
Analyze the mufti's methodology
Understand the tahqiq from Fath al-Qadir: the mufti must have ijtihad and knowledge of people's conditions, and the kaffarah requires complete offense.
The mufti looks at whether the person's nature is repulsed by the meat.
4
Understand the tarjih mechanism
If the nature is repulsed, adopt Abu Yusuf (no breaking even if large); otherwise adopt Zufar (breaking in both cases).
This shows how custom and individual condition affect the fatwa.
5
Apply the rule to the general principle
Relate the example to the rule: custom is accepted except when it contradicts shari'ah, like taxes and usury.
The mufti, qadi, and mujtahid must know people's conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العرف إذا خالف الشريعة وقال في "فتح القدير" في باب ما يوجب القضاء والكفارة، من كتاب الصوم عند قول "الهداية": "ولو أكل لحماً بين أسنانه لم يفطر، وإن كان كثيراً يفطر، وقال زفر يفطر في الوجهين". ما نصه: "والتحقيق أن المفتي في الوقائع لا بد له من ضرب اجتهاد ومعرفة بأحوال الناس، وقد عرف أن الكفارة تفتقر إلى كمال الجناية، فينظر إلى صاحب الواقعة إن كان ممن يعاف طبعه ذلك أخذ بقول أبي يوسف، وإن كان ممن لا أثر لذلك عنده، أخذ بقول زفر". وفي "تصحيح العلامة قاسم فإن قلت: قد يحكون أقوالاً من غير ترجيح، وقد يختلفون في التصحيح؟ قلت يعمل بمثل ما علموا من اعتبار تغير العرف، وأحوال الناس، وما هو الأرفق بالناس، وما ظهر عليه التعامل، وما قوي وجهه، ولا يخلو الوجود من تمييز هذا حقيقةً لا ظناً بنفسه، ويرجع من لم يميز إلى من يميّز لبراءة ذمته. فهذا كله صريح فيما قلنا من العمل بالعرف ما لم يخالف الشريعة، كالمكس والربا ونحو ذلك. فلا بد للمفتي والقاضي بل والمجتهد من معرفة أحوال الناس، وقد قالوا ومن جهل بأهل زمانه فهو جاهل. وقدّمنا أنهم قالوا: يفتي بقول أبي يوسف فيما يتعلق بالقضاء؛ لكونه جرّب الوقائع، وعرف أحوال الناس. وفي البحر عن مناقب الإمام محمد للكردري كان محمد يذهب إلى الصباغين، ويسأل عن معاملتهم، وما يديرونها فيما بينهم.
Custom when it contradicts Shari'ah. And he said in Fath al-Qadir in the chapter on what necessitates qada' and kaffarah from the book of fasting, concerning the statement of al-Hidayah: "If one ate meat between his teeth, he does not break his fast, and if it is a large amount, he breaks his fast, and Zufar said he breaks in both cases." Its text: "The verification is that the mufti in incidents must have a type of ijtihad and knowledge of the conditions of people, and it is known that kaffarah requires complete offense; so he looks at the person of the incident: if he is one whose nature is repulsed by that, he takes the statement of Abu Yusuf, and if he is one for whom there is no effect of that, he takes the statement of Zufar." And in Tashih al-Allama Qasim: "If you say: They may relate statements without preference, and they differ in correction? I say: One acts according to what they have learned from considering changes in custom, conditions of people, what is more convenient for people, what is apparent in transactions, and what has a strong basis; and existence is not free from distinguishing this in reality, not by conjecture, and one who cannot distinguish refers to one who can to absolve his responsibility." So all this is explicit in what we said: acting according to custom as long as it does not contradict Shari'ah, like the customs of illegal taxes and usury and the like. Hence, the mufti, the judge, and even the mujtahid must have knowledge of the conditions of people, and they said: "Whoever is ignorant of the people of his time is ignorant." And we have already mentioned that they said: One gives fatwa according to the statement of Abu Yusuf in matters related to judiciary because he experienced incidents and knew the conditions of people. And in al-Bahr from Manaqib al-Imam Muhammad by al-Kardari: "Muhammad used to go to the dyers and ask about their transactions and what they conduct among themselves."
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents the rasm rule that custom ('urf) is to be followed as long as it does not contradict explicit shari'ah texts. The author supports this with an example from Fath al-Qadir regarding the ruling on eating meat stuck between teeth while fasting. According to the Hidayah, if a person eats meat between his teeth during fasting, he does not break his fast unless the amount is large, in which case he breaks. Imam Zufar holds that he breaks the fast in both cases. The tahqiq from Fath al-Qadir states that a mufti must exercise ijtihad and understand people's conditions. He should look at the individual: if the person's nature would find that meat repulsive, then he should adopt Abu Yusuf's view (that it does not break the fast even if large), otherwise adopt Zufar's view (that it breaks in both cases). This shows that custom and individual circumstances affect the fatwa. The text then quotes from Tashih al-Allama Qasim that when scholars relate different opinions without tarjih, one should act according to what they have learned about changes in custom, people's conditions, what is more convenient for people, and what is commonly practiced. The passage concludes that this all confirms the principle: custom is acted upon as long as it does not contradict shari'ah, like customs involving bribery (al-maks) and usury (al-riba) which are rejected. Therefore, a mufti, qadi, and even mujtahid must know the conditions of the people. It then mentions that it was previously stated that one should give fatwa according to Abu Yusuf's opinion in matters related to judiciary because he experienced many cases and knew people's conditions. It also cites from Al-Bahr that Imam Muhammad used to go to dyers and ask about their transactions.

Key Terms
العرف (al-'urf): Customary practice that is considered in fatwa as long as it does not contradict shari'ah.
المفتي (al-mufti): One who issues fatwas; must have ijtihad and knowledge of people's conditions.
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): Independent reasoning to derive rulings, especially in applying custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tahqiq in Fath al-Qadir, if a fasting person eats meat stuck between his teeth and his nature is repulsed by it, which imam's view should the mufti adopt?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad
D) Imam Zufar

Key Takeaway
Custom is a valid source for fatwa, but only when it does not contradict shari'ah; the mufti must assess individual and customary conditions in applying rulings.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Kitman al-Fatwa: Withholding a Ruling to Prevent Oppression
Explains why a true kharaj ruling is withheld to prevent oppression

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify situations where a Hanafi mufti may withhold a fatwa to prevent harm and explain the principle of kitman al-fatwa with reference to kharaj.

Core Idea
A true ruling may be withheld if its declaration enables oppression.

The Hanafi school upholds the truth of its rulings, but it also demands that the mufti consider real-world consequences. In the case of kharaj al-a'la, the ruling is legally correct, yet scholars deliberately refrain from issuing it as a fatwa. Why? Because revealing it would arm oppressive officials with a tool to extort farmers. This lesson explores that delicate balance between legal correctness and practical justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the withheld ruling
Find the specific fiqh rule that is being withheld: the landowner planting a low-value crop while capable of a high-value one must pay kharaj at the higher rate.
This is a pure tax rule, not a general worship ruling.
2
Understand the rationale for withholding
The scholars feared that if this ruling became widely known, every oppressive official would claim that any land could yield high-value crops, leading to unjust taxation.
The harm (mafsada) of declaring the ruling outweighs the benefit (maslaha).
3
Analyze the objection and response
An objection from al-'Inayah asks how concealment can be lawful when the tax is obligatory. The answer: because the oppression that follows would be worse.
This is a classic dar' al-mafasid muqaddam 'ala jalb al-masalih.
4
Extract the rasm al-mufti principle
The mufti must not be rigid (junud) but must consider custom ('urf), clear indicators (qara'in), and the social reality to avoid causing injustice.
This is a direct application of maqasid al-shari'ah within fatwa.
5
Apply to similar modern scenarios
Think of a ruling that, if publicly issued, would enable harm – e.g. a fatwa about a valid sale that could be used to justify usury indirectly. The mufti may withhold it and guide the questioner differently.
The principle is general, not limited to kharaj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالوا: إذا زرع صاحب الأرض أرضه ما هو أدنى مع قدرته على الأعلى، وجب عليه خراج الأعلى، قالوا: وهذا يعلم ولا يفتى به؛ كي لا يتجرأ الظلمة على أخذ أموال الناس". قال في "العناية": وردّ بأنه كيف يجوز الكتمان؟ ولو أخذوا كان في موضعه؛ لكونه واجباً. وأجيب بأنا لو أفتينا بذلك لادّعى كل ظالم في أرض ليس شأنها ذلك أنها قبل هذا كانت تزرع الزعفران مثلا، فيأخذ خراج ذلك، وهو ظلم وعدوان. وكذا قال في فتح القدير : قالوا: لا يفتى بهذا؛ لما فيه من الظلمة على أموال المسلمين؛ إذ يدّعي كل ظالم أن الأرض تصلح الزراعة الزعفران ونحوه، وعلاجه صعب. فقد ظهر لك أن جمود المفتي أو القاضي على ظاهر المنقول، مع ترك العرف والقرائن الواضحة والجهل بأحوال الناس يلزم منه حقوق كثيرة، وظلم خلق كثيرين.
They said: When the owner of land plants in his land the lowest [crop] while capable of the highest, the kharaj of the highest is obligatory upon him. They said: This is known but no fatwa is given on it, lest the oppressors become audacious in taking people's property. In al-'Inayah, it was objected: How can concealment be permissible? Even if they took it, it would be in its place, because it is obligatory. And it was answered: If we gave fatwa on that, every oppressor would claim concerning land not of that nature that previously it used to grow saffron, for example, and he would take the kharaj of that, which is oppression and transgression. Similarly, in Fath al-Qadir, they said: No fatwa is given on this because of the oppression on the property of Muslims; every oppressor claims that the land is suitable for cultivating saffron and the like, and its remedy is difficult. Thus it has become clear to you that the rigidity of the mufti or judge on the apparent transmitted text, while abandoning custom, clear circumstantial evidence, and ignorance of people's conditions, results in many lost rights and oppression of many people.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a practical fatwa principle. The rule: if a landowner plants a low-value crop despite capacity for a high-value one, he is liable for kharaj at the higher rate. However, the scholars said: this ruling is known but not given as a fatwa. Why? Because if it were publicly pronounced, every oppressive official would claim that any land yields high-value crops, demanding inflated taxes, leading to widespread injustice. The objection raised in al-'Inayah is that withholding a true ruling seems wrong, especially if the tax is obligatory. The answer is that the harm caused by its declaration outweighs the benefit. The text warns that a mufti or judge who rigidly follows transmitted rulings without considering custom, clear evidence, and people's circumstances causes many rights to be lost and oppresses many. This is a rasm rule: the mufti must consider real-world consequences.

Key Terms
خراج الأعلى (kharaj al-a'la): The higher kharaj applicable to land capable of high-value crops
كتمان الفتوى (kitman al-fatwa): The act of withholding a known ruling to prevent harm
جمود (jumud): Rigid adherence to transmitted texts without consideration of context

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do the Hanafi scholars say 'this is known but no fatwa is given' regarding the kharaj of the higher crop?
A) Because the ruling is weak in the madhhab
B) Because issuing it would enable oppressors to unjustly extract money from farmers
C) Because the ruling applies only to sugar cane, not to saffron
D) Because the mufti is not allowed to issue fatwa on taxation matters

Key Takeaway
A mufti must balance legal correctness with practical consequences, and may withhold a fatwa if public knowledge would cause harm.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
12 min
Customary Practice Specifies Texts and Overrides Analogy
Explains the qawida on custom and provides two furuat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal maxim 'التعامل حجة يترك به القياس ويخص به الأثر' and apply it to contracts like istisna' and the weaver case.

Core Idea
Custom is a proof: it can specify a general text and override qiyas, but never abandon the text entirely.

The passage from al-Dhakhirah establishes a key principle of Hanafi mufti methodology: customary practice (ta'amul) can be used to specify the scope of an authoritative text (athar) and to set aside analogical reasoning (qiyas). However, this is not an abandonment (tark) of the text; it is a specification (takhsis) that leaves the text intact for other contexts. The example of istisna' (manufacturing contract) illustrates how a widespread custom permits what would otherwise be prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida
Read the maxim: 'التعامل حجة يترك به القياس ويخص به الأثر'. Customary practice is a proof; by it qiyas is abandoned and the text is specified.
This is a sughra (minor) qawida specific to transactions.
2
Understand its scope
The qawida applies in contracts and transactions, particularly Ijarat and Buyu'. It does not apply to acts of worship (ibadat).
Custom influences rulings where texts are general and custom provides specificity.
3
Apply to the weaver case
The text prohibits 'qafiz al-tahhan' (a type of uncertain rental). The weaver case is analogous. Custom of Balkh permitted the weaver contract, specifying the prohibition to the miller case only.
This is takhsis, not tark, because the prohibition is still applied to the miller.
4
Apply to istisna'
Istisna' (manufacturing contract) is prohibited by the general text on selling what one does not possess. Widespread custom made it permissible, specifying the text to exclude istisna'.
The text is not abandoned; it still applies to other sales.
5
Note the condition of widespread custom
The custom must be widespread (ta'amul 'amm), not limited to one town. Otherwise, it cannot specify due to doubt.
This condition is crucial for the validity of takhsis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواز تخصيص الأثر بالتعامل لا تركه] قال في "الذخيرة" في الفصل الثامن من الإجارات في مسألة ما لو دفع إلى حائك غزلا لينسجه بالثلث ومشايخ بلخ كنصير بن يحيى، ومحمد بن سلمة، وغيرهما، كانوا يُجيزون هذه الإجارة في الثياب؛ لتعامل أهل بلدهم في الثياب، والتعامل حجة يترك به القياس، ويخص به الأثر. وتجويز هذه الإجارة في الثياب للتعامل، بمعنى تخصيص النص الذي وَرَدَ في قفيز الطحان؛ لأن النص ورد في قفيز الطحان لا في الحائك، إلا أن الحائك نظيره فيكون وارداً فيه دلالةً، فمتى تركنا العمل بدلالة هذا النص في الحائك، وعملنا بالنص في قفيز الطحان كان تخصيصا لا تركاً أصلا، وتخصيص النص بالتعامل جائز. ألا ترى أنا جوّزنا الاستصناع للتعامل، والاستصناع بيع ما ليس عنده، وإنه منهي عنه وتجويز الاستصناع بالتعامل تخصيص منا للنص الذي ورد في النهي عن بيع ما ليس عند الإنسان، لا ترك للنص أصلا؛ لأنا عملنا بالنص في غير الاستصناع. قالوا: وهذا بخلاف ما لو تعامل أهل بلدة قفيز الطحان؛ فإنه لا يجوز، ولا تكون معاملتهم معتبرة؛ لأنا لو اعتبرنا معاملتهم كان تركاً للنص أصلا، وبالتعامل لا يجوز ترك النصّ أصلا، وإنما يجوز تخصيصه، ولكن مشايخنا لم يجوزوا هذا التخصيص؛ لأن ذلك تعامل أهل بلدة واحدة، وتعامل أهل بلدة واحدة لا يخص الأثر؛ لأن تعامل أهل بلدة إن أن يجوز التخصيص، فترك التعامل من أهل بلدة أخرى يمنع التخصيص، فلا يثبت التخصيص بالشك، بخلاف التعامل في الاستصناع، فإنه وجد في البلاد كلها. انتهى كلام "الذخيرة".
[Permissibility of specifying the effect by custom, not abandoning it] He said in al-Dhakhirah, in the eighth chapter of Ijarat, regarding the case where one gives yarn to a weaver to weave for a third, and the scholars of Balkh like Nasir ibn Yahya, Muhammad ibn Salama, and others, used to permit this ijarah for clothes due to the custom of the people of their town in clothes, and custom is a proof by which analogy is abandoned and the text is specified. The permission of this ijarah for clothes due to custom means specifying the text that came regarding the qafiz of the miller; because the text came regarding the qafiz of the miller, not the weaver, except that the weaver is its analogue so it applies by implication. So when we abandon acting on the implication of this text regarding the weaver and act on the text regarding the qafiz of the miller, it is specification, not abandonment at all, and specifying the text by custom is permissible. Do you not see that we permitted istisna' due to custom, and istisna' is selling what one does not possess, and it is prohibited, and our permitting istisna' by custom is a specification from us of the text prohibiting selling what one does not possess, not an abandonment of the text at all, because we act on the text in other than istisna'. They said: This is contrary to if the people of a town transacted regarding the qafiz of the miller; then it is not permissible, and their transaction is not considered, because if we considered their transaction it would be an abandonment of the text entirely, and by custom it is not permissible to abandon the text entirely, but only to specify it. However, our mashayikh did not permit this specification because that is the custom of the people of one town, and the custom of one town does not specify the text, because if the custom of one town could permit specification, then the lack of custom from another town would prevent specification, so specification is not established by doubt, unlike the custom in istisna', which existed in all cities. End of the words of al-Dhakhirah.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule: customary practice (ta'amul) can serve as a basis to specify (takhsis) an authoritative text (athar) but never to completely abandon it. The author quotes al-Dhakhirah to illustrate. The case involves a weaver who receives yarn to weave for a share (one-third). Hanafi scholars of Balkh permitted this contract based on local custom, even though analogous reasoning (qiyas) would prohibit it (since it resembles a prohibited contract). The key distinction: custom leads to specification of the text, not abrogation. For example, the text prohibits the qafiz of the miller (a type of rental with uncertain measure), and the weaver case is analogous. By allowing the weaver contract due to custom, they are specifying the prohibition to only the miller case, not abandoning it. Similarly, istisna' (manufacturing contract) is permitted despite the general prohibition of selling what one does not possess, again by specifying the prohibition through universal custom. The exception: if a custom is limited to one town, it cannot specify a text because the absence of that custom in other towns creates doubt. Only a widespread (universal) custom can specify. Thus, Hanafi methodology maintains the authority of texts while accommodating customary practice within strict limits.

Key Terms
تعامل (ta'amul): Customary practice of people in transactions, recognized as a legal proof.
أثر (athar): An authoritative text (hadith or legal ruling) that is being specified by custom.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general text to exclude some cases based on custom, without abrogation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Hanafi scholars of Balkh permit the weaver contract despite its resemblance to the prohibited qafiz al-tahhan?
A) They considered the prohibition weak and abandoned it.
B) They used local custom to specify the text, leaving the prohibition intact for the miller.
C) They argued the text was abrogated by later practice.
D) They said the analogy was flawed and the weaver case is not covered.

Key Takeaway
Custom only specifies texts; it never abandons them, and the custom must be widespread to have that effect.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Limited Custom Does Not Specify a Text
Explains the exception to the qawida: local custom does not specify texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a custom limited to one town cannot specify an authoritative text, and apply the maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' to this context.

Core Idea
Local custom cannot specify a text; only widespread custom has that authority.

The passage from al-Dhakhirah establishes an important exception to the qawida on custom. While widespread custom can specify texts, a custom confined to a single town cannot. The reason is that the lack of that custom elsewhere introduces doubt, and the certainty of the text cannot be overridden by doubt. This lesson focuses on that exception and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the istithna
The exception: custom limited to one town does not specify the text. The passage says: 'تعامل أهل بلدة واحدة لا يخص الأثر'.
This is a dabt (restrictive sub-maxim) on the main qawida.
2
Understand the reasoning
If local custom could specify, then the absence of that custom in another town would prevent specification, creating uncertainty. Certainty (the text) cannot be removed by doubt.
The maxim: 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' (Certainty is not removed by doubt).
3
Apply to qafiz al-tahhan scenario
If only one town practices the miller custom, the text remains binding universally because the custom is not widespread.
The text's prohibition is certain; local custom creates doubt, so the prohibition stays.
4
Contrast with widespread custom
Istisna' custom existed in all cities, so it could specify the text. Local custom lacks that universality.
Widespread custom provides near-certainty.
5
Extract the legal principle
For a custom to specify a text, it must be 'amm (universal) or at least predominant. Any lesser custom leaves the text in full force.
This protects the sanctity of revealed texts from being undermined by local practices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواز تخصيص الأثر بالتعامل لا تركه] قال في "الذخيرة" في الفصل الثامن من الإجارات في مسألة ما لو دفع إلى حائك غزلا لينسجه بالثلث ومشايخ بلخ كنصير بن يحيى، ومحمد بن سلمة، وغيرهما، كانوا يُجيزون هذه الإجارة في الثياب؛ لتعامل أهل بلدهم في الثياب، والتعامل حجة يترك به القياس، ويخص به الأثر. وتجويز هذه الإجارة في الثياب للتعامل، بمعنى تخصيص النص الذي وَرَدَ في قفيز الطحان؛ لأن النص ورد في قفيز الطحان لا في الحائك، إلا أن الحائك نظيره فيكون وارداً فيه دلالةً، فمتى تركنا العمل بدلالة هذا النص في الحائك، وعملنا بالنص في قفيز الطحان كان تخصيصا لا تركاً أصلا، وتخصيص النص بالتعامل جائز. ألا ترى أنا جوّزنا الاستصناع للتعامل، والاستصناع بيع ما ليس عنده، وإنه منهي عنه وتجويز الاستصناع بالتعامل تخصيص منا للنص الذي ورد في النهي عن بيع ما ليس عند الإنسان، لا ترك للنص أصلا؛ لأنا عملنا بالنص في غير الاستصناع. قالوا: وهذا بخلاف ما لو تعامل أهل بلدة قفيز الطحان؛ فإنه لا يجوز، ولا تكون معاملتهم معتبرة؛ لأنا لو اعتبرنا معاملتهم كان تركاً للنص أصلا، وبالتعامل لا يجوز ترك النصّ أصلا، وإنما يجوز تخصيصه، ولكن مشايخنا لم يجوزوا هذا التخصيص؛ لأن ذلك تعامل أهل بلدة واحدة، وتعامل أهل بلدة واحدة لا يخص الأثر؛ لأن تعامل أهل بلدة إن أن يجوز التخصيص، فترك التعامل من أهل بلدة أخرى يمنع التخصيص، فلا يثبت التخصيص بالشك، بخلاف التعامل في الاستصناع، فإنه وجد في البلاد كلها. انتهى كلام "الذخيرة".

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule: customary practice (ta'amul) can serve as a basis to specify (takhsis) an authoritative text (athar) but never to completely abandon it. The author quotes al-Dhakhirah to illustrate. The case involves a weaver who receives yarn to weave for a share (one-third). Key Terms
تعامل عام (ta'amul 'amm): Widespread customary practice found in many regions.
تعامل خاص (ta'amul khas): Custom limited to a specific locality or group.
شك (shakk): Doubt that prevents certainty from being overturned.

Checkpoint
Why cannot a custom limited to one town specify a text?

A custom must be widespread to specify a text; a local custom introduces doubt and cannot override the certainty of the text.

The Hanafi Rule on Weak Opinions: Prohibition and Necessity Exception
Rasm al-mufti rule on weak opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on acting upon weak (marjuh) opinions by identifying when necessity permits an exception and distinguishing between Hanafi and Shafi'i positions.

Core Idea
A weak (marjuh) opinion is like nothing in the madhhab—prohibited to act upon unless necessity forces the hand.

In the Hanafi madhhab, the mufti is bound to follow the preponderant (rajih) opinion. But what happens when a weak (marjuh) opinion exists? This lesson unpacks the rasm al-mufti rule that prohibits acting upon the marjuh, the reasoning behind it (like abrogation), and the sole exception of necessity. It also clarifies the difference from the Shafi'i view, which allows following a weak opinion for personal practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Rule
From the text, determine whether the Hanafi madhhab prohibits acting upon a marjuh opinion in fatwa, personal practice, or both.
The author cites 'Allamah Qasim that giving judgment and fatwa according to marjuh is against consensus.
2
Understand the Reasoning: 'Like Non-Existent'
Explain why the marjuh is considered like non-existent or abrogated, and when this reasoning fully applies (e.g., when a mujtahid retracts or temporal precedence is known).
The author clarifies that even without literal abrogation, the established correct opinion makes the other like non-existent.
3
Note the Exception: Necessity (Darurah)
Identify the sole exception to the rule: necessity. Find the concrete example given: the traveler adopting Abu Yusuf's weak opinion to avoid doubt (riba).
The example involves ghusl for a wet dream, but the key is the necessity of avoiding riba.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i Position
Contrast the Hanafi rule with the Shafi'i view as reported by al-Subki: Shafi'is allow following a weak opinion for oneself but not in fatwa or judgment.
The Hanafi response is that the consensus on prohibition targets caprice (tashahhi), not necessity.
5
Apply to a New Scenario
Given a hypothetical case, decide whether a mufti may use a marjuh opinion, citing the rule and exception.
Practice distinguishing between caprice and genuine necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

٨٤
الإفتاء والعمل على الضعيف
في رسالة جعلتها شرحا لهذا البيت وضمنتها بعض ما عنيت، وسميتها "نشر العرف في بناء بعض الأحكام على العُرف"، فمن رام الزيادة
على ذلك، فليرجع إلى ما هنالك.
ولا يجوز بالضعيف العمل
إلا لعامل له
ضروره
ولا به يجاب من جاء يسأل
أو من له معرفة مشهوره
لكنما القاضي به لا يقضي وإن قضى فحكمه لا يمضي لا سيّما قضاتُنا إذْ قُيّدوا براجح المذهب حين قلدوا وتم ما نظمته في سلك والحمد لله ختام مسك الإفتاء والعمل على الضعيف]
قدمنا أول الشرح عن العلامة قاسم: أن الحكم والفتيا بما هو مرجوح
خلاف الإجماع، وأن المرجوح في مقابلة الراجح بمنزلة العدم، والترجيح بغير مرجّح في المتقابلات ممنوع، وأن من يكتفي بأن يكون فتواه أو عمله موافقا لقول أو وجه في المسألة، ويعمل بما شاء من الأقوال والوجوه من

مقتضى مذهب الشافعي كما قاله السبكي: منع العمل بالقول المرجوح

شرح عقود رسم المفتي
٨٥
الإفتاء والعمل على الضعيف
في القضاء والإفتاء دون العمل لنفسه. ومذهب الحنفية: المنع عن المرجوح لنفسه؛ لكون المرجوح صار منسوخا".
حتى
قلت التعليل بأنه صار منسوخاً إنما يظهر فيما لو كان في المسألة قولان، رجع المجتهد عن المجتهد عن أحدهما ، أو علم تأخر أحدهما عن الآخر، وإلا . فلا، كما لو كان في المسألة قول لأبي يوسف وقول لمحمد، فإنه لا يظهر فيه النسخ، لكن مراده أنه إذا صحح أحدهما صار الآخر بمنزلة المنسوخ. وهو معنى ما مر من قول العلامة قاسم: "إن المرجوح في مقابلة الراجح بمنزلة العدم".
ثم إن ما ذكره السبكي من جواز العمل بالمرجوح في حق نفسه عند الشافعي، مخالف لما مر عن العلامة ،قاسم، وقدّمنا مثله أول الشرح عن فتاوى ابن حجر" من نقل الإجماع على عدم الإفتاء والعمل بما شاء الأقوال، إلا أن يقال : المراد بالعمل الحكم والقضاء، وهو بعيد. والأظهر في الجواب أخذاً من التعبير بالتشهي مهما أراد من الأقوال في أي وقت أراد، أما لو عمل بالضعيف في بعض الأوقات لضرورة اقتضت ذلك، فلا يمنع منه.
من
وعليه يحمل ما تقدم عن الشرنبلالي: "من" أن مذهب الحنفية المنع"، بدليل أنهم أجازوا للمسافر والضيف الذي خاف الريبة أن يأخذ بقول أبي يوسف بعدم وجوب الغسل على المحتلم الذي أمسك ذكره عند ما أحس بالاحتلام إلى أن فترت شهوته ثم أرسله، مع أن قوله هذا
خلاف الراجح في المذهب، لكن أجازوا الأخذ به للضرورة.
Commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti (page 84): [Section on] Issuing Fatwa and Acting on the Weak. In a treatise I made as a commentary on this verse and included some of what I intended, and I named it 'Nashr al-'Urf fi Bina' Ba'd al-Ahkam 'ala al-'Urf'. Whoever seeks more than that, let him refer to that work. [Poetic lines:] 'And it is not permissible to act upon the weak, except for one who acts out of necessity. Nor is it answered to the one who comes asking, or to one who knows its well-known [opinion]. But the judge does not judge by it, and if he judges, his judgment does not pass, especially our judges, since they are bound by the preponderant of the madhhab when they follow. And what I composed is completed in a string, and praise be to God, the seal of musk.' [Commentary:] We presented earlier, at the beginning of the commentary, from 'Allamah Qasim: that giving judgment and fatwa according to a preponderated (marjuh) opinion is against consensus, and that the marjuh is in contrast to the rajih, like non-existence, and that preponderance without a preponderator in contradictory matters is prohibited, and that whoever is content that his fatwa or action be in agreement with a saying or a view in the matter, and he acts as he wishes from the sayings and views without consideration of preponderance, has been ignorant and violated consensus.' And we presented there similar from the fatawa of 'Allamah Ibn Hajar, but also there: Imam al-Subki said in his fatawa on waqf: 'It is permissible to follow the weak view in itself with respect to action in one's own right, not in fatwa and judgment, for Ibn al-Salah reported consensus that it is not permissible.' And 'Allamah al-Shurunbulali said in his treatise 'al-'Iqd al-Farid fi Jawaz al-Taqlid': 'The implication of the Shafi'i madhhab, as al-Subki said, is the prohibition of acting upon the weak view in judgment and fatwa, but not in action for oneself. And the Hanafi madhhab: prohibition of the marjuh for oneself, because the marjuh has become abrogated.' Until I said: The reasoning that it has become abrogated is only apparent when there are two sayings in the matter, and the mujtahid retracted one of them, or it is known that one is later than the other. Otherwise, no, as when there is a saying of Abu Yusuf and a saying of Muhammad in a matter, for abrogation is not apparent there. But his intent is that when one is established as correct, the other becomes like the abrogated. That is the meaning of what passed from the statement of 'Allamah Qasim: 'Indeed, the marjuh is in contrast to the rajih like non-existence.' Then what al-Subki mentioned of the permissibility of acting upon the marjuh in one's own right according to the Shafi'is is contrary to what passed from 'Allamah Qasim, and we presented its like at the beginning of the commentary from the fatawa of Ibn Hajar, reporting consensus on the prohibition of giving fatwa and acting upon whatever sayings one desires, except that it may be said: the intended meaning of 'action' is judgment and adjudication, which is far [from the meaning]. And the more apparent in the answer, taking from the expression 'whimsically' (al-tashahhi), is [that acting upon] whatever sayings [one desires] at any time [one desires] is prohibited, but if one acts upon the weak in some times due to a necessity that requires that, then it is not prevented. And upon this is interpreted what preceded from al-Shurunbulali: 'the Hanafi madhhab is prohibition,' as evidence that they allowed the traveler and the guest who feared doubt (al-riba) to take the saying of Abu Yusuf that ghusl is not obligatory for the one who has a wet dream and held his penis when he felt the dream until his desire subsided and then released it, even though his saying is contrary to the preponderant in the madhhab, but they allowed taking it due to necessity.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti discussion on the permissibility of issuing fatwa or acting upon weak (marjuh) opinions in the Hanafi madhhab. The author begins by citing earlier scholars, particularly 'Allamah Qasim, who stated that giving judgments and fatwas according to a marjuh opinion is contrary to ijma (consensus). The marjuh is regarded as non-existent in contrast to the rajih. Anyone who picks and chooses opinions without considering tarjih (preponderance) is ignorant and violates ijma. Then the author quotes Imam al-Subki (Shafi'i) who permitted following a weak view for one's own personal practice but not in fatwa or judgment, and Ibn al-Salah reported ijma that it is not permissible. Al-Shurunbulali clarifies the difference: Shafi'is prohibit for judgment/fatwa but allow for personal practice; Hanafis prohibit even for oneself because the marjuh is considered abrogated. The author then refines the abrogation reasoning: it only applies when a mujtahid retracts one opinion or temporal precedence is known; for differences like between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, abrogation is not literal, but when one is established as correct, the other becomes like the abrogated. The author resolves the apparent contradiction with Subki by explaining that the consensus on prohibition applies to acting out of caprice, not to cases of necessity. An example is given: the Hanafis allowed a traveler or guest who feared doubt (riba) in a transaction to adopt Abu Yusuf's weak opinion that ghusl is not required when one holds the penis after feeling the onset of a wet dream until desire subsides, despite it being contrary to the rajih. Thus, the Hanafi position is strict prohibition except in cases of genuine necessity.

Key Terms
المرجوح (al-marjuh): The opinion that is outweighed or weaker in evidence, considered like non-existent in the madhhab.
الراجح (al-rajih): The preponderant opinion that is to be relied upon in fatwa and judgment.
التشهي (al-tashahhi): Acting out of personal whim or caprice, choosing opinions arbitrarily without regard to tarjih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab as explained in this passage, which of the following is true regarding acting upon a weak (marjuh) opinion?
A) It is always permissible for personal practice, just like the Shafi'i madhhab allows.
B) It is prohibited in fatwa but allowed for one's own practice without restriction.
C) It is prohibited for both fatwa and personal practice, except in cases of necessity.
D) It is permissible for judges but not for muftis.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi madhhab, a weak (marjuh) opinion is practically non-existent and cannot be used in fatwa or personal practice unless a genuine necessity (darurah) demands it.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Rule on Weak Opinions (Marjuh) in Hanafi Iftaa
Explains Hanafi rule on weak opinions and necessity exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi prohibition on acting upon weak opinions for oneself and apply the necessity exception with reference to the traveler/guest example.

Core Idea
A weak opinion is like abrogated — prohibited to act upon unless necessity demands.

This lesson examines a foundational rasm al-mufti rule: the Hanafi position on acting upon weak (marjuh) opinions. The school generally prohibits a mufti or individual from following a weak opinion for personal practice, treating it as legally non-existent. However, an exception exists when necessity (darurah) arises. We will explore the reasoning, the dispute with the Shafi'i school, and a concrete case from al-Shurunbulali that illustrates the exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline rule
State the general Hanafi ruling: acting upon a weak opinion for oneself is prohibited because the weak opinion is like abrogated (mansukh) or non-existent when compared to the strong opinion.
The term 'naskh' here is analogical; the weak opinion loses legal effectiveness.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
Analyze the ta'lil: the weak opinion becomes like abrogated only if the mujtahid retracted it or if one opinion is later. If the two opinions come from different imams (e.g., Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad), there is no actual abrogation, but the weak one is still treated as non-existent in contrast to the strong.
This refinement by the author clarifies the scope of the analogy.
3
Contrast the Shafi'i position
Note that al-Subki reports the Shafi'i school permits acting upon weak opinions for oneself. The Hanafi response distinguishes between personal practice (which is prohibited) and judicial ruling (qada') – but the text argues that the better interpretation is that one cannot arbitrarily pick opinions at any time.
The phrase 'whimsically' (التشهي) is key: arbitrary choice is banned, not necessity-driven choice.
4
Apply the necessity exception
Learn the exception: if necessity (darurah) prompts acting upon a weak opinion, it is allowed. The example: a traveler or guest who fears suspicion (riybah) may follow Abu Yusuf's weak opinion that ghusl is not required after a wet dream, even though the stronger opinion requires ghusl.
The exception preserves the school's methodology while responding to real-world hardship.
5
Synthesize for fatwa practice
Combine the rule and exception: a mufti must not issue fatwa based on weak opinions arbitrarily, but when a genuine necessity arises and no stronger alternative is possible, the weak opinion may be relied upon for that specific case.
This is a key tarjih mechanism in Rasm al-Mufti: the hierarchy of opinions and the exception for darurah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإفتاء والعمل على الضعيف في القضاء والإفتاء دون العمل لنفسه. ومذهب الحنفية: المنع عن المرجوح لنفسه؛ لكون المرجوح صار منسوخا. حتى قلت التعليل بأنه صار منسوخاً إنما يظهر فيما لو كان في المسألة قولان، رجع المجتهد عن أحدهما، أو علم تأخر أحدهما عن الآخر، وإلا فلا، كما لو كان في المسألة قول لأبي يوسف وقول لمحمد، فإنه لا يظهر فيه النسخ، لكن مراده أنه إذا صحح أحدهما صار الآخر بمنزلة المنسوخ. وهو معنى ما مر من قول العلامة قاسم: "إن المرجوح في مقابلة الراجح بمنزلة العدم". ثم إن ما ذكره السبكي من جواز العمل بالمرجوح في حق نفسه عند الشافعي، مخالف لما مر عن العلامة قاسم، وقدّمنا مثله أول الشرح عن فتاوى ابن حجر من نقل الإجماع على عدم الإفتاء والعمل بما شاء من الأقوال، إلا أن يقال: المراد بالعمل الحكم والقضاء، وهو بعيد. والأظهر في الجواب أخذاً من التعبير بالتشهي مهما أراد من الأقوال في أي وقت أراد، أما لو عمل بالضعيف في بعض الأوقات لضرورة اقتضت ذلك، فلا يمنع منه. وعليه يحمل ما تقدم عن الشرنبلالي: أن مذهب الحنفية المنع، بدليل أنهم أجازوا للمسافر والضيف الذي خاف الريبة أن يأخذ بقول أبي يوسف بعدم وجوب الغسل على المحتلم الذي أمسك ذكره عند ما أحس بالاحتلام إلى أن فترت شهوته ثم أرسله، مع أن قوله هذا خلاف الراجح في المذهب، لكن أجازوا الأخذ به للضرورة.
Issuing fatwa and acting upon the weak opinion in judicial matters and fatwa, not for one's own personal practice. The Hanafi school prohibits the weak opinion for oneself because the weak opinion becomes like abrogated. Until I said: The reasoning that it becomes abrogated is only evident in a case where there are two opinions, and the mujtahid retracted one, or it is known that one is later than the other. Otherwise no, such as if there is a statement of Abu Yusuf and a statement of Muhammad, then abrogation is not evident, but his intent is that when one is considered correct, the other becomes like abrogated. This is the meaning of what passed from Allamah Qasim: 'The weak opinion in contrast to the strong is like non-existence.' Then what al-Subki mentioned about permissibility of acting upon the weak opinion in one's own right according to al-Shafi'i, contradicts what passed from Allamah Qasim, and we presented earlier at the beginning of the commentary from the fatwas of Ibn Hajar that consensus is transmitted on not giving fatwa and acting upon any opinions arbitrarily, unless it is said that 'acting' means judicial decision and verdict, which is far-fetched. The more apparent in the answer, taking from the expression 'whimsically', is that he may take any opinion whenever he wishes. However, if one acts upon the weak opinion at certain times due to a necessity that required it, then it is not prohibited. And upon this is based what passed from al-Shurunbulali: that the Hanafi school prohibits, as evidenced by their permitting the traveler and the guest who fears suspicion to take the opinion of Abu Yusuf regarding the non-obligation of ghusl for one who had a wet dream, who held his penis when he felt the dream until his desire subsided and then released it, even though this opinion is against the stronger opinion in the school, but they allowed it due to necessity.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage clarifies a rasm rule for muftis: acting upon weak opinions. The Hanafi school generally prohibits a person from acting upon a weak opinion for his own personal practice, because a weak opinion is treated as if abrogated. The author refines this: the idea of abrogation applies if the mujtahid retracted an opinion or if one opinion is later. If it's just two opinions from different imams (like Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad), there's no abrogation. However, the weak one is still like non-existent when compared to the strong. The author then contrasts the Shafi'i position as reported by al-Subki, which allows acting upon weak opinions for oneself. The Hanafi response: the word 'acting' in the alleged consensus means judicial ruling, not personal practice, but this is weak. The better interpretation is that one cannot arbitrarily pick any opinion at any time, but if necessity prompts acting upon a weak opinion, it is allowed. An example is given from al-Shurunbulali: a traveler or guest who fears suspicion (of being impure) may follow Abu Yusuf's less strict opinion on ghusl after a wet dream, even though the stronger opinion is to do ghusl. This is allowed due to necessity.

Key Terms
المرجوح (al-marjuh): The weak or outweighed opinion in a legal dispute, as opposed to the strong (rajih) opinion.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation; the weak opinion is treated as if it were abrogated in the sense of being legally ineffective.
التشهي (al-tashahhi): Acting upon whims or arbitrarily choosing an opinion without methodological justification.
الضرورة (al-darurah): Necessity that permits an exception to the general rule; here, allows acting upon a weak opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it permissible for a person to act upon a weak (marjuh) opinion for his own personal practice?
A) Whenever he prefers it over the strong opinion.
B) Only when there is a necessity (darurah) that requires it.
C) In all cases, as long as it is from an imam of the school.
D) Only in judicial matters (qada'), not in personal worship.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits acting upon weak opinions for oneself unless necessity arises, and this principle is applied in fatwa by allowing exceptions like the traveler case.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling on Issuing Fatwa and Acting Upon Weak Opinions in Necessity
Explains the permissibility of following weak opinions when necessary, with examples from Hanafi fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition of necessity (darurah) that permits issuing fatwa with a weak (da'if) opinion, and apply the qawida 'يجوز الإفتاء والعمل بالضعيف عند الضرورة' to specific fiqh cases.

Core Idea
Weak opinions are permissible in necessity, but not in normal circumstances — the school's hierarchy protects rigor while allowing ease.

This lesson explores a critical principle in Hanafi ifta: when can a mufti depart from the well-known (mashhur) ruling and rely on a weak (da'if) opinion? Through examples from Imam al-Marghinani and personal experience of the author, you will see how necessity (darurah) acts as a gateway to otherwise restricted opinions, while the default rule remains to follow the strong, established views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principal qawida
Extract the core maxim from the passage: 'يجوز الإفتاء والعمل بالضعيف عند الضرورة'. This is the key rule governing the entire discussion.
The qawida is sughra (minor) and operates within the broader maxims of 'المشقة تجلب التيسير' and 'الضرر يزال'.
2
Understand the condition: necessity (darurah)
Analyze what constitutes darurah here. The passage includes both existential threat (kufr) and significant hardship (haraj) as seen in the cauterized pea case. Note that personal difficulty suffices if it prevents normal practice.
Darurah is broader than life-threatening situations; it includes extreme hardship.
3
Recognize the default rule (istithna)
The default is that weak opinions are not acted upon. The exception is only when necessity exists. Identify the istithna in the qawida panel: 'لا يفتى بالضعيف ولا يعمل به في غير الضرورة'.
This safeguards the school's reliability while allowing flexibility.
4
Apply to the furuat (branches)
Work through the three examples: (1) blood from wounds not nullifying wudu (Taharah), (2) author's personal case of cauterized pea (Taharah), (3) not declaring a Muslim kafir even with weak narration (Aqidah). For each, confirm the presence of necessity and the weak opinion.
Each furu' demonstrates the qawida in action.
5
Evaluate the authority and practice
Note that the weak opinion must come from a qualified imam (like al-Marghinani) capable of takhrij and tas-hih. The mufti must only use it when genuinely needed, and the individual who followed it in necessity should later make up (qada) if possible, as the author did.
Adab al-mufti requires caution and not making a habit of weak opinions.

من هذا القبيل ما ذكره الإمام المرغيناني صاحب "الهداية" في كتابه "مختارات النوازل" - وهو كتاب مشهور ينقل عنه شراح "الهداية" وغيرهم حيث قال في فصل النجاسة: "والدم إذا خرج من القروح قليلا قليلا غير سائل فذاك ليس بمانع وإن كثر. وقيل: لو كان بحال لو تركه لسال، يمنع ثم أعاد المسألة في نواقض الوضوء، فقال: "ولو خرج منه شيء قليل ومسحه بخرقة حتى لو ترك يسيل لا ينقض. وقيل: إلخ.

وقد راجعت نسخة أخرى، فرأيت العبارة فيها كذلك. ولا يخفى أن المشهور في عامة كتب المذهب هو القول الثاني المعبّر عنه بـ"قيل". وأما ما اختاره من القول الأول، فلم أَرَ من سبقه إليه، ولا من تابعه عليه بعد المراجعة الكثيرة، فهو قول شاذ ولكن صاحب "الهداية" إمام جليل من أعظم مشايخ المذهب، من طبقة أصحاب التخريج والتصحيح، كما مر فيجوز للمعذور تقليده في هذا القول عند الضرورة، فإن فيه توسعة عظيمة لأهل الأعذار كما بينته في رسالتي المسماة "الأحكام المخصصة بكي الحمّصة".
وقد كنت ابتليتُ مدّة بكي الحمّصة، ولم أجد ما تصح به صلاتي على مذهبنا بلا مشقة إلا على هذا القول؛ لأن الخارج منه وإن كان قليلاً لكنه لو ترك يسيل، وهو نجس وناقض للطهارة على القول المشهور خلافا لما قاله بعضهم كما قد بيّنته في الرسالة المذكورة، ولا يصير به صاحب عذر؛ لأنه يمكن دفع العذر بالغسل والربط بنحو جلدة مانعة للسيلان عند كل صلاة، كما كنت أفعله، ولكن فيه مشقة وحرج عظيم، فاضطررت إلى تقليد هذا القول، ثم لما عافاني الله تعالى منه أعدت صلاة تلك المدة. والله تعالى الحمد.
وقد ذكر صاحب "البحر" في الحيض في بحث ألوان الدماء أقوالا ضعيفةً، ثم قال: وفي "المعراج" عن فخر الأئمة: لو أفتى مفت بشيء من هذه الأقوال في مواضع الضرورة طلباً للتيسير كان حسنا.
وبه علم أن المضطرّ له العمل بذلك لنفسه كما قلنا، وأن للمفتي الإفتاء به للمضطر. فما مرّ من أنه ليس له العمل بالضعيف ولا الإفتاء به محمول على غير موضع الضرورة، كما علمته من مجموع ما قررناه. والله تعالى أعلم. وينبغي أن يلحق بالضرورة أيضا ما قدمناه من أنه لا يفتى بكفر مسلم، في كفره اختلاف ولو رواية ضعيفة فقد عدلوا عن الإفتاء بالصحيح؛ لأن الكفر شيء عظيم.
And it is appropriate that issuing fatwa and acting upon the weak (opinion) is of this type: what Imam al-Marghinani, author of al-Hidayah, mentioned in his book Mukhtarat al-Nawazil - and it is a well-known book from which the commentators of al-Hidayah and others transmit - where he said in the chapter on impurity: 'Blood that comes out of wounds little by little, not flowing, that is not a preventer even if abundant. And it was said: if it was in a state that if left alone it would flow, it prevents.' Then he repeated the issue in the nullifiers of wudu, saying: 'And if something little comes out of it and he wipes it with a cloth such that if left it would not flow, it does not nullify. And it was said: etc.' ... And I have checked another copy, and I saw the wording in it likewise. And it is not hidden that the well-known in all the books of the school is the second statement expressed by 'it was said.' As for what he chose of the first statement, I have not seen anyone before him nor anyone after him upon it after extensive review, so it is a rare (shadhdh) statement, but the author of al-Hidayah is a great imam from the greatest shaykhs of the school, from the class of those capable of derivation and correction (takhrij and tas-hih), as has passed, so it is permissible for one with an excuse to follow him in this statement at times of necessity, for in it there is great leniency for people with excuses, as I have explained in my treatise named 'al-Ahkam al-Mukhassasah bi Kayy al-Himmisah.' And I was afflicted for a period with the cauterization of a pea, and I did not find anything by which my prayer would be valid according to our school without hardship except upon this statement; because what comes out even if little, but if left it flows, and it is impure and nullifies purification according to the well-known statement, contrary to what some have said as I have explained in the mentioned treatise, and he does not become a person of excuse because the excuse can be removed by washing and binding with something like a skin that prevents flow at every prayer, as I used to do, but therein is great hardship and difficulty, so I was compelled to follow this statement. Then when Allah Almighty cured me of it, I repeated the prayers of that period. Praise be to Allah Almighty. And the author of al-Bahr mentioned in menstruation, in the discussion of the colors of blood, weak statements, then said: 'In al-Mi'raj from Fakhr al-A'immah: If a mufti issues a fatwa with something from these statements in places of necessity seeking facilitation, it is good.' And by this it is known that the one in need may act upon that for himself as we said, and that the mufti may issue a fatwa with it for the one in need. So what has passed that he may not act upon the weak nor issue a fatwa with it is applied to other than a place of necessity, as you know from the totality of what we have stated. And Allah Almighty knows best. And it is appropriate to also annex to necessity what we have presented: that a Muslim is not declared an unbeliever if there is difference regarding his unbelief, even if a weak narration, for they have turned away from issuing fatwa with the correct because unbelief is a great matter.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the science of Usul al-Iftaa regarding the permissibility of issuing fatwa and acting upon weak opinions within the Hanafi school under conditions of necessity. The author begins by stating the principle: it is appropriate that fatwa and action may be based on weak opinions. He then provides an example from Imam al-Marghinani's Mukhtarat al-Nawazil, where two opinions are cited regarding blood from wounds: the first (chosen by al-Marghinani) states that non-flowing blood does not prevent or nullify wudu even if abundant; the second (the well-known, ‘qil’) states that if left to flow it would nullify. The author notes that the second opinion is the mashhur in the school, while the first is shadhdh (rare). However, because al-Marghinani is a great imam of the school, capable of takhrij and tas-hih, his opinion may be followed by a person with an excuse (ma‘dhur) in times of necessity, as it provides great leniency. The author then shares a personal example: he was afflicted with a cauterized pea (kayy al-himmisa) that would ooze blood. According to the well-known opinion, the blood would invalidate his wudu and he could not be considered a person of excuse (sahib ‘udhr) because he could bind it to prevent flow. However, binding before every prayer caused him great hardship, so he was forced to follow the weak opinion. After recovery, he repeated those prayers. Then he cites al-Bahr al-Ra’iq, quoting Fakhr al-A’imma: it is good for a mufti to give fatwa with weak opinions in places of necessity to facilitate ease. The conclusion is that the general prohibition against acting on or issuing fatwa with weak opinions applies only in non-necessity situations. Finally, a special annex: when there is any difference of opinion (even a weak narration) regarding the kufr of a Muslim, the fatwa must avoid declaring kufr, because kufr is a grave matter. This is an application of the same principle: taking the weaker opinion to avoid greater harm.

Key Terms
الضعيف (al-Da'if): A weak opinion within the Hanafi school, i.e., one that is not mashhur (well-known) or is considered shadhdh (rare), but may still be valid in terms of ijtihad.
الضرورة (al-Darurah): A situation of extreme hardship or necessity that justifies departing from the standard ruling to avoid harm or excessive difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is it permissible to issue a fatwa based on a weak (da'if) opinion according to this passage?
A) Whenever the mufti prefers it over the strong opinion.
B) Only when the weak opinion is the majority view.
C) In cases of necessity (darurah) to provide ease.
D) Only if the weak opinion is the most authentic in hadith.

Key Takeaway
Weak opinions are permissible in necessity to remove hardship, as demonstrated by blood nullification and kufr cases, but the default remains to follow the well-known (mashhur) opinions.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
